<Text>Been going to Upper Bidwell Park/Monkey Face/Lower Bidwell/Horseshoe "Lake" (more of a pond now) and "The Dirt Road" all my life because I grew up right at the trail head to the "Dirt Road." It's been no doubt a big part of what keeps me in love with chico...and the girl I still love from high school for almost 20 years.

The trails are awesome for hiking and biking. They take you to fresh cold running creek water that consists of huge swimming holes that are famous, the top of the mountain for beautiful views, a frisbee golf course, the iconic "Monkey face", golf course and the planetarium.

Since the  virus, the trails have been extremely overcrowded, lots of trash and dog poop. I'm guessing it's because of the gyms closed. If you decide to enjoy the adventures of all that outdoor chico life has to offer, then make sure to pick up what you drop. Keep chico clean, natural and beautiful and it will return the favor.  üòé< /Text><Pictures>None< /Pictures><Resp>None</Resp>< Gmap_id>

During the summer I decided to get some bids before winter returned. He corroborated what Alex suspected was shoddy installation of two new windows and a new slider by the previous owner.  The same afternoon, Alex came out and really spent time discussing a solution and a very detailed plan of action that was easy for me to visualize.  The following morning I received an email from Alex that thoroughly depicted the plan including proposal, materials and timeframe, from start to finish and even included possible contingency plans, in case when further into the walls, the damage was more than anticipated, along with what I thought was a fair estimate for a lot of work that included pulling up and re-stretching carpet, mold remediation, removing and reinstalling base board and exterior siding and trim, sealing badly installed windows and slider, caulking and painting inside and out.

<Text>My wife and I contracted with Cobex Construction Group to make improvements, upgrades and repairs to our home in the Ridgewiew Neighborhood El Dorado Hills.  The house is a one of one design by the architect owner that we have owned for 4 years.

My review will be in several parts because  the projects will take time during the winter months.  I can't say enough good things about their estimating and contracting process, workmanship and follow up on all aspects of the work.

From the beginning, getting an initial estimate and many discussions about what would look best  from design through construction was informative and excellent.  Everything was covered, no guess work and full disclosure if there were issues spotted and how we wanted to proceed.

The project consisted of updating the kitchen with new Quartzite surfaces and some appliances.  The Quartzite is a natural stone from Brazil and the backslash is glass subway tile that we purchased from Bedrosians.  We had the electrical switches and plugs updated with Legrand Adorna.  A new Sharp drawer microwave, Bosch dishwasher and a GE Profile cook top hood. The microwave required cabinet modifications and the hood required cutting the stone surround to fit the vent which it was done perfectly.  The cabinet modifications were completed with precision and even the touch up paint for the farm house cabinets matched perfectly.

Our kitchen had solid granite counter tops that were installed when the house was new, 2001.  The counter tops had seams in the granite that went through the sinks and were not level or really match up.

The COBEX crew came in an put down heavy duty paper to protect our Hickory floors. They put up a sheet plastic wall around the kitchen to keep the dust from going into the dining area and family room.  They removed all of the granite counter tops, the island and back splash behind the cook top.

Afterward, everything was spotlessly vacuumed up and taken away.  Next they put down new plywood counter top base and backer board for the tile back splash, nearly 70 SQ feet.  They made all of their templates and off to the fabricator.

The fabricator returned and removed more of the stone surround for the cook top and one wall cabinet.  He had fabricated the counters all, without any seams.  He and his crew worked tirelessly to fit these huge pieces in perfectly.  FYI.  The quartzite is a very hard natural stone and it took extra time to cut and shape.  The tile setter did an amazing job with the glass subway tile and moving the electrical boxes to a high level on the wall.  It sparkles and looks fantastic.

We stood in the kitchen just admiring the stone and the craftsmanship.  We had a party two weeks ago and everyone was impressed with the kitchen and their amazing craftsmanship.

We had all of the rain gutters replaced as the old one were in poor shape.  The COBEX construction group had the sub contractor measure everything and consulted me all along the way.  After the gutters were installed, Alex from COBEX walked the entire perimeter with the gutter fabricator to insure everything was perfect.

We also had the eaves inspected for dry rot, the COBEX crew came though, stripped back 2 rows of tile, removed the damaged areas and replaced everything very nicely.  Alex walked the entire roof with the sub-contractor to follow up on all of the repairs and to insure everything was perfect.

Last will be the upgrade of the 2 HVAC units in a very tight a difficult area.

I'll be writing as these next projects get completed.  With the rainy weather it will take a little longer.

Alex, Vaz and the COBEX team are fantastic and respond to every email or question we have had.<//Text><pictures>None<//pictures><response>{'time': 1544569370642, 'text': 'We are so pleased to hear that you are satisfied with our work, thank you for choosing Cobex Construction to complete your project San!'}</response>< gmap_id>

<Time>1527170906909</Time><rating>1< /rating><text>My inital visit to Prestige Auto was pleasant, albeit suspect. I got what I thought was a decent deal on my car (ignoring the fact that they didn't know what year it was until they printed off the paperwork, after which they told me that it was not a 2007 but rather a 2012) and was financed through them.
Upon leaving the dealership, I found that any bump in the road caused the car to swerve, so I alerted the dealership and they paid to "fix" it. The people at the repair shop told me that the last time someone repaired the suspension on the car, they repaired it incorrectly, and the car was actually missing a part. So much for their thorough pre-sale inspection, right? So whatever, they fix it and I'm fine with that.
Shortly after this, I take the car on a trip of 1500 miles, which shouldn't have been a problem for this car, as it was presented as being in such good condition. However, at mile 600, my car starts acting up on the freeway. I step out to see that both of my rear tires are completely bald and flat. I paid for a tow truck to take me in to the nearest town to get it checked out and repaired. When I go to pick up the car, he shows me that the suspension components are so weak that he's able to compress them completely with his bare hands. Thats strike 3 for Prestige.
Fast forward about a month, I haven't been billed a single payment for the car, and Prestige calls me up saying "Hey, we were able to get you a bwtter interest rate for the car, so we're gonna overnight you a new contract so you can make lower monthly payments. I'm stoked, so I agree. They send me the contract, I send it back, and await the first bill. Fast forward another month, and I get a call from the lender saying they can no longer honor the loan because they overnighted me the contract rather than having me fill it out on site. I call Prestige to ask what the deal is, they give me an "oh well" and start getting aggressive, saying I have to get the car back to them on my dime (no cheap feat, as I had moved to Texas for work). I decide to get aggressive back, and as soon as I threaten legal action, they're suddenly able to make a deal with me, where I go through a lender of my choice and have them send the money to Prestige.

So here's a recap:
1. Sold me an incorrectly-labeled car with poorly repaired suspension (negligent and dangerous)
2. Had my car repaired poorly which resulted in a middle-of-nowhere break down (expensive and dangerous)
3. Sent me a contract to sign at my residence, not realizing that this would, in fact, nullify the contract (negligent)
4. Blamed me for the loan falling through and aggressively pressured me to send the car back to them on my own dime (bad business practices)
5. Magically found a solution when I refused to back down and let them know what kind of legal resources I had at my disposal (lack of integrity)

All in all, I wish I had just sent the car back and that I had taken these guys to court to pay for the vehicle transport fees. I would die before I'd recommend Prestige Auto to anyone.<//text>< pics>

However, they do provide a fantastic shopping experience. You browse their app/ catalogue, you order online and relax. If you subscribe to Prime, most stuff is shipped for free and often arrives within 24 hours. When it arrives at the Hub Locket, you get a confirmation email with a barcode. Hop on the bus, 15 minutes to USC campus (for me).
When you enter the Hub there is an array of lockers. You click a button on the email you received on your cellphone which generates a QR code and tells you which locker your items are in. Place your phone against a scanner, the locker door slides open and that's it! Painless. You can take up to 15 days before you retrieve your package if necessary. < Review>
The University Village has potential. What's hindering it is that there's a lot of stores that aren't open yet and a lot of empty store spaces. The ones that are available provide a lot. Most of the restaurants are pricey. There's a couple that are reasonable. There's always lots of parking it's underground. You get either one hour if you shop at one of the places, or two hours if you go to a restaurant. There's a large grassy area to play with in the front and even larger one in the back.< /Review>
